    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5554854320857112679">The son of a prosperous landowner and a former slave, Paul-Edward Logan is unlike any other boy he knows. His white father has acknowledged him and raised him openly-something unusual in post-Civil War Georgia. But as he grows into a man he learns that life for someone like him is not easy. Black people distrust him because he looks white. White people discriminate against</span>
  <span id="freeText5554854320857112679" style="display:none">The son of a prosperous landowner and a former slave, Paul-Edward Logan is unlike any other boy he knows. His white father has acknowledged him and raised him openly-something unusual in post-Civil War Georgia. But as he grows into a man he learns that life for someone like him is not easy. Black people distrust him because he looks white. White people discriminate against him when they learn of his black heritage. Even within his own family he faces betrayal and degradation. So at the age of fourteen, he sets out toward the only dream he has ever had: to find land every bit as good as his father's, and make it his own. Once again inspired by her own history, Ms. Taylor brings truth and power to the newest addition to the award-winning Logan family stories.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5554854320857112679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2774134496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2774134496" />
    <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt"><img alt="Rebecca McNutt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602390057p2/36977686.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2774134496?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca McNutt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca McNutt" href="/user/show/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt">Rebecca McNutt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=history">history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=civil-war">civil-war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36977686-rebecca-mcnutt?shelf=african-american">african-american</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2774134496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8645126588180106140"><i>The Land</i> is a book which tackles a very heavy subject, something which even today still causes controversy, stigma and prejudice. Set in a post-Civil War time of "free" black people, for young Paul Logan, he finds that even in the aftermath of slavery, a time when he's supposed to feel equal, he's still facing judgment based on his skin and his heritage. In a world that doesn't give you anywhere to belong, how do you find out where you're supposed to go? Well, luckily Paul has dreams to hold ont</span>
  <span id="freeText8645126588180106140" style="display:none"><i>The Land</i> is a book which tackles a very heavy subject, something which even today still causes controversy, stigma and prejudice. Set in a post-Civil War time of "free" black people, for young Paul Logan, he finds that even in the aftermath of slavery, a time when he's supposed to feel equal, he's still facing judgment based on his skin and his heritage. In a world that doesn't give you anywhere to belong, how do you find out where you're supposed to go? Well, luckily Paul has dreams to hold onto, and with determination and hope, he sets forth to carve out a piece of that dream for himself.<br /><br />I loved Paul as a character; he's not only inspirational in his words and actions, but even in the face of the cruellest judgment, he doesn't let this destroy his spirit. I also think that, in our current time of progressive attempts, we often forget that the legacy of racial prejudice seen here in this story is such a strong legacy that it still affects us even today, and if we can't remember it, we'll only keep repeating it in however subtle or strong a form it takes. Paul is a reminder to all readers though that no human being deserves to be degraded, devalued or ignored - we all have dreams regardless of our race, and Paul is ready to prove to himself and the rest of the world that he has value and worth just like anybody else. I was a little surprised by his father, who does such things as separating Paul from the dinner table in the presence of guests, but I suppose in his own way he was only trying to protect his son. Supporting characters like Mitchell and Sam bring out deeper accompanying themes, making for a complex and very strong story. <br /><br />*Just a warning to readers - there are some racial slurs in this book in the context of its setting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8645126588180106140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Saba" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4075951-saba"><img alt="Saba" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1303861558p2/4075951.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166222680?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Saba" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Saba" href="/user/show/4075951-saba">Saba</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166222680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15724514992544649387">I am not exaggerating when I say this is one of the greatest books ever! The Land is about an African American boy named Paul Edward Logan, who lives on his white fathers plantation. Paul lives in the time of racism, slaves, and disrespect of black men and women. Even his very own father treats him differently than Pauls white brothers he cannot eat at the table when there are guests. Nor can he talk to white men the way they treat him. Paul begins to realize the truth of it all. However, he doe</span>
  <span id="freeText15724514992544649387" style="display:none">I am not exaggerating when I say this is one of the greatest books ever! The Land is about an African American boy named Paul Edward Logan, who lives on his white fathers plantation. Paul lives in the time of racism, slaves, and disrespect of black men and women. Even his very own father treats him differently than Pauls white brothers he cannot eat at the table when there are guests. Nor can he talk to white men the way they treat him. Paul begins to realize the truth of it all. However, he does not give up his dream to own his own land. He does not lose faith, even when his father denies him an opportunity to race a horse for cash. Denial only pushes him to accept the offer, but the owner of the horse refuses to pay him his winnings. Mitchell, his personal bodyguard, decides to take matters into his own hands and makes them running for their lives. The Land takes the readers on a journey of Pauls determination, hard work, and his daring and desperate decisions.<br />One reason I absolutely love this book is because of the plot! The way Paul and African Americans are treated helps me understand what it was like for people, like Paul during the 1800s. This book helps me realize how hard it was back then to treat others respectfully while they mistreat you, to try to be quiet when a white man was speaking! For example, in the book, Paul is not allowed to hit his brother when he has done something wrong because he is white. It makes me think about how unfair it was a century ago. People were treated unjust because of the color of their skin! I now appreciate my life much, much more, knowing how many lifestyles used to be.<br />In addition to this, I love the suspense! There is always something exciting happening from the horse race to the fights where Mitchell, Pauls bodyguard protects him. What makes this book so fascinating is the fact that there is always something incredible, simply amazing happening. This makes me want to read more! Not only is it entertaining, but also this book raises many intriguing questions. For example, what is going to happen to Paul, what dramatic decision will he make now, and how is Pauls father going to react to this chaos? As you can tell, many questions arise. This is one great aspect of The Land.<br />I recommend this book to readers who enjoy books based on history something that actually happened. The Land is based on true facts how people were considered, how lifestyles were for African Americans, and how there were many unjust, unfair laws. This book has a wonderful plot, which is not only entertaining, but also educational. You would have to read it yourself!<br />I can understand why this book won the Coretta Scott King Award! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15724514992544649387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14223547006403389534">Let's just say that I planned on not really enjoying this book. Mostly because I hate to say it, but I judged it by its cover and its title. I just sort of thought it had little to offer me, a 30-something woman, but I knew that the high goodreads rating couldn't be that far off, and so I cracked it open. Besides, I had to finish reading it before my students did.<br/><br/>It surprised me right off with its story of Paul-Edward Logan, son to a white plantation owner and a slave. I almost thought I had mad</span>
  <span id="freeText14223547006403389534" style="display:none">Let's just say that I planned on not really enjoying this book. Mostly because I hate to say it, but I judged it by its cover and its title. I just sort of thought it had little to offer me, a 30-something woman, but I knew that the high goodreads rating couldn't be that far off, and so I cracked it open. Besides, I had to finish reading it before my students did.<br /><br />It surprised me right off with its story of Paul-Edward Logan, son to a white plantation owner and a slave. I almost thought I had made an error in judgement in choosing it for my 7th graders. How could Taylor possibly cover this controversial part of our history in terms that they could understand? She did. At some points I gasped out loud at the harshness of the reality of this world I couldn't imagine. And yet it was so different than other books written about this time. It focused on hard work and it didn't have any easy answers. It made me so angry for Paul at times.<br /><br />I gave it four out of five stars only because I found some of the story, although based on the author's own ancestors, to be a bit too convenient. I was right there with Paul-Edward when he realized the man Sam Perry was talking about was Mitchell and I felt so sorry for Paul. I sort of liked that twist. I didn't like it when it all worked out. The tragedy seemed far too convenient for Paul and the storyline. It felt like a bit of a betrayal.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14223547006403389534" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16038117774950815604">This book is a must-read as a prequel to "Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry." I'm not sure how I came upon this book before I found it sitting on my bookshelf, but I'm so glad it's in my possession. This book taught me much about family, loyalty, dreams and sacrifice. This is a story of a man, Paul Logan, who is both black and white, a dangerous combination back in the late 1800s. His white father and brothers, however, treat him like he's no different, but throughout the course of his life, events h</span>
  <span id="freeText16038117774950815604" style="display:none">This book is a must-read as a prequel to "Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry." I'm not sure how I came upon this book before I found it sitting on my bookshelf, but I'm so glad it's in my possession. This book taught me much about family, loyalty, dreams and sacrifice. This is a story of a man, Paul Logan, who is both black and white, a dangerous combination back in the late 1800s. His white father and brothers, however, treat him like he's no different, but throughout the course of his life, events have a way of changing one brother's view of him and Paul runs away. His dream has always been to own land, and he saves money through his work with his friend Mitchell. They eventually end up in an area where Paul finds his dream land. Through the subsequent years, Paul, along with Mitchell and other new found friends, painstakingly work for another piece of land while he waits for the dream land to become available to buy. When it becomes available, a few mishaps come along that nearly prevent him from getting it. Although it was predictable that he would obtain the land, the way he gets it is miraculous, brought on by his and others' faith in God. <br /><br />It was a beautiful, moving story that is actually taken from Mildred Taylor's family history. I recommend this to anyone.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3137107894" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3137107894" />
    <a title="Gabriella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14674200-gabriella"><img alt="Gabriella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491520533p2/14674200.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabriella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabriella" href="/user/show/14674200-gabriella">Gabriella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14674200-gabriella?shelf=southern-lit">southern-lit</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3137107894" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16098221197585206151">Five stars, each and every time. Mildred D. Taylor’s prequel to the Logan family saga introduces readers to Paul-Edward Logan, a man of quiet strength, resolute morals, and audible ambition. (He may be better known, in certain circles, generations, and fandoms, as Cassie Logan’s grandfather.) The Land is a masterfully-paced story that reminds you of the deep pleasure found in hard work aimed towards an honest end, and it’s one that I have a deep history with. <br/><br/>The Land was one of the first books </span>
  <span id="freeText16098221197585206151" style="display:none">Five stars, each and every time. Mildred D. Taylor’s prequel to the Logan family saga introduces readers to Paul-Edward Logan, a man of quiet strength, resolute morals, and audible ambition. (He may be better known, in certain circles, generations, and fandoms, as Cassie Logan’s grandfather.) The Land is a masterfully-paced story that reminds you of the deep pleasure found in hard work aimed towards an honest end, and it’s one that I have a deep history with. <br /><br />The Land was one of the first books my mom read to my siblings and me in our home in South Carolina, and I remember re-reading it several times during the move. At the time, I did not know (or currently do not remember knowing) that it is a semi-biographical account of Mildred Taylor’s great-grandfather’s pivotal journey from bondage to ownership, and his exploits along the way. Taylor fills in the expectations, dreams, and gambles of her ancestors with such consideration that you’d believe she was along for the ride. It’s a testament to her great-grandfather’s determination, to her great-grandmother and father’s storytelling, but ultimately to her own craft, that Paul-Edward’s journey is one that feels as true as that of my own ancestors’. <br /><br />As part of our 2020 reading challenges, my mom and I are revisiting the older works of her favorite YA author, Mildred D. Taylor, and will soon get to read All the Days Past, All the Days to Come for the very first time. My mom has loved the Logan story for decades, partially because of its similarities to her paternal side of the family, the Taylors. The emphasis on ownership (particularly of land), the urge to record our stories (both orally as well as in writing), and the unconditional bond of family are lessons I’ve learned by watching my cousins, uncles, and mother in action over the years. Every descendant has their own unique application of their family’s legacy, I am incredibly thankful to read where Ms. Taylor has taken the fruits of her great-grandparents’ labor. She is an encouragement to become more diligent about cultivating the seeds planted by relatives before me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16098221197585206151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_331838513" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/331838513" />
    <a title="Liza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5726003-liza"><img alt="Liza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435768262p2/5726003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/331838513?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liza" href="/user/show/5726003-liza">Liza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5726003-liza?shelf=favorite">favorite</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5726003-liza?shelf=classroom-library">classroom-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5726003-liza?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5726003-liza?shelf=young-adult-historical-fiction">young-adult-historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer331838513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2748228853177266493">I was afraid this book would go down the path of so many other historical novels where the tone tends to be preachy or worse white-washed. This novel, thankfully, is none of that. This is the story of Paul Logan, a son of a former slave and white man. <br/><br/>This story isn't simply about life after the Civil War and the racial conflicts that arose. This is Paul Logan's story and the many challenges he faced in order to gain personal achievement. Taylor did a wonderful job of weaving in historical accur</span>
  <span id="freeText2748228853177266493" style="display:none">I was afraid this book would go down the path of so many other historical novels where the tone tends to be preachy or worse white-washed. This novel, thankfully, is none of that. This is the story of Paul Logan, a son of a former slave and white man. <br /><br />This story isn't simply about life after the Civil War and the racial conflicts that arose. This is Paul Logan's story and the many challenges he faced in order to gain personal achievement. Taylor did a wonderful job of weaving in historical accuracy with compassion and grace. There are times you will cringe when you read about how Caucasians treated all minorities in general, be they biracial or otherwise. There are racial slurs, but like the author explained, within its context, the words were needed to preserve what truly was a horrifying time in American history.<br /><br />Paul Logan's story begins from the time he is a boy and is bullied by a young black boy named Mitchell, who would later on become a dear friend. There are terrible lessons to be learned about what it meant to be black and the obstacles and lack of opportunities they faced. Taylor does not downplay the random violence that many black people faced and the racial injustices they faced collectively. <br /><br />Once Paul Logan becomes an adult you are pained to learn that he has learned not to trust white men and not to become beholden to them even if they offer their help. It's a horrible lesson he had to learn, with a bittersweet background that led him to that particular personal philosophy.<br /><br />There is romance in the book, though sweet and short. <br /><br />Paul Logan's journey was transformational; the challenges he went through in order to achieve his goal, land in this instance, made the overall reading experience enjoyable and the ending was absolutely perfect. It was not a sugary sweet "happily ever after," and once you learn how much Taylor extracted from her family history to write this novel the characters and story become that much more alive and powerful.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2748228853177266493" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_519942346" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/519942346" />
    <a title="Mrs. Berger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16875456-mrs-berger"><img alt="Mrs. Berger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1360260496p2/16875456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/519942346?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mrs. Berger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mrs. Berger" href="/user/show/16875456-mrs-berger">Mrs. Berger</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer519942346" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14917583146902312191">I was pleasantly surprised by how much I actually liked this book. However, I was even more amazed by how much my 8th grade students enjoyed it. Not only did Taylor give us a peek into our country's history following the Civil War, but she did so by sharing her own family's experiences of it. <br/><br/>Right from the beginning of the book she makes us care about Paul Edward and all of those connected to him. She hooks the reader in by showing that he is a flawed individual who is continuously trying to fi</span>
  <span id="freeText14917583146902312191" style="display:none">I was pleasantly surprised by how much I actually liked this book. However, I was even more amazed by how much my 8th grade students enjoyed it. Not only did Taylor give us a peek into our country's history following the Civil War, but she did so by sharing her own family's experiences of it. <br /><br />Right from the beginning of the book she makes us care about Paul Edward and all of those connected to him. She hooks the reader in by showing that he is a flawed individual who is continuously trying to figure out who he actually is and where he really belongs. Many of the obstacles Paul must overcome resonate with many readers even though the events occurred 150+ years ago. It opens the readers eyes to the idea that even though many things may have progressed during this time the relationships and the problems that may arise between family members and friends remain the same, just the cause may be different. <br /><br />I would recommend this book without hesitation. If you have read "Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry" this is a must read prequal to it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14917583146902312191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3551538856" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3551538856" />
    <a title="Nancy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14386326-nancy"><img alt="Nancy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551041023p2/14386326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3551538856?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nancy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nancy" href="/user/show/14386326-nancy">Nancy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14386326-nancy?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14386326-nancy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3551538856" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13986664766009688578">After writing many books about the Logan family of Mississippi, author Mildred D Taylor wrote a prequel, using her real great-grandfather's story as the basis for it. *Some spoilers* Paul Edward is born right before the Civil War to a white father and a slave mother who was half Native American. Paul Edward was raised by both parents, and his father acknowledged his Black children, as his white wife had died so he lived openly with Paul's mother. His older white brothers accepted him and his sis</span>
  <span id="freeText13986664766009688578" style="display:none">After writing many books about the Logan family of Mississippi, author Mildred D Taylor wrote a prequel, using her real great-grandfather's story as the basis for it. *Some spoilers* Paul Edward is born right before the Civil War to a white father and a slave mother who was half Native American. Paul Edward was raised by both parents, and his father acknowledged his Black children, as his white wife had died so he lived openly with Paul's mother. His older white brothers accepted him and his sister, but eventually, the brother closest in age turned against Paul, siding with two racist white friends. When his father whips him for striking his brother, Paul decides to leave Georgia and strike out on his own in Texas with a childhood friend Mitchell. After a few years, Paul finds himself in Mississippi and falls in love with a piece of land that is for sale. He and Mitchell earn money by logging and meet Caroline, whom Mitchell marries. After Mitchell is killed by a drunk white man, Paul eventually marries a pregnant Caroline and raises Mitchell's son as his own in addition to the children they would have together (their youngest son David would become Cassie's father from Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry). The heartbreaking sacrifices that were made to obtain The Land show why it was so important to keep it in the family, and we meet younger versions of characters that would be in other Logan books. <br /><br />This was a fascinating book as it pulled from Taylor's family, and included a family tree to keep track of the generations. Paul Edward's life as being multi-racial showed that despite him only being a quarter Black, and could pass as white if he had chosen to do so, life in that era forced him into a category in which he was discriminated against. He had to deal with looking too white for Blacks and being too Black for whites. The family relationships in his childhood were layered, for although his mother had clearly been forced into a sexual relationship with his father during slavery, choose to stay with him even after she was granted her freedom. Paul's white brothers and Black sister had different levels of connection to him in later years, and in the family tree you could see all their names in either Paul's children or grandchildren. His family bonds, although severed for a time, lived on. Family life can be messy during the best of times, but when racism is added to the mix, you can understand why Paul forged his own path and built a loving family that would thrive in the years to come.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13986664766009688578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14336925537712731706">Paul-Edward will stay with me for a very long time. My heart broke, sang, I held my breath, I got mad, I watched him pull through. Mildred D Taylor shows all sides of her characters and doesn't shy away from hard subjects or complex feelings. Right to the end I wasn't exactly sure what was going to happen and I was with her the whole way as she told the story. Much of it (as well as the other Logan family books) was based on true experiences lived by members of her own family, and I think that c</span>
  <span id="freeText14336925537712731706" style="display:none">Paul-Edward will stay with me for a very long time. My heart broke, sang, I held my breath, I got mad, I watched him pull through. Mildred D Taylor shows all sides of her characters and doesn't shy away from hard subjects or complex feelings. Right to the end I wasn't exactly sure what was going to happen and I was with her the whole way as she told the story. Much of it (as well as the other Logan family books) was based on true experiences lived by members of her own family, and I think that comes through in their jumping off the page, and feeling like real, full fleshed out people.<br /><br />Thanks to Adira because I didn't know the extent of the Logan Family series up until a few months ago and now I'm on a quest to read them all. &lt;3</span>

<div id="review_64075993" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64075993" />
    <a title="Destiny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1728861-destiny"><img alt="Destiny" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64075993?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Destiny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Destiny" href="/user/show/1728861-destiny">Destiny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780439442411" href="/book/show/2628565-the-land">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1728861-destiny?shelf=10th-grade-bookshelf">10th-grade-bookshelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1728861-destiny?shelf=advisory-summer-assignment">advisory-summer-assignment</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64075993" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15503721797624025832">The Land<br/>Midred D. Taylor<br/>375 pgs.<br/><br/>Have you ever suffered from identity crisis? Have you ever thought am I to call myself black or am I to call myself white? Have you ever let society choose your ethnicity for you? In the land Paul-Edward Logan faced all of these questions. Paul suffered from identity crisis all throughout his childhood. His mother was a former slave and black and his father was the owner of the planation, the master to the slaves and white. Paul himself was born into slavery and h</span>
  <span id="freeText15503721797624025832" style="display:none">The Land<br />Midred D. Taylor<br />375 pgs.<br /><br />Have you ever suffered from identity crisis? Have you ever thought am I to call myself black or am I to call myself white? Have you ever let society choose your ethnicity for you? In the land Paul-Edward Logan faced all of these questions. Paul suffered from identity crisis all throughout his childhood. His mother was a former slave and black and his father was the owner of the planation, the master to the slaves and white. Paul himself was born into slavery and he was a slave until after the American Civil war. Paul childhood was a very big question that he could never answer; am I black or am I white? Society choose him as black. But he didn't want to believe that because he lived a white life that his three white brothers lived. He was taught how to read, wirte and figure by his father and his brothers. He was well clothed. He knew how to ride horses really well and tame them too. Paul was very gifted.. But it wasn;t until three occassions in his life that paul realized that he was black and no matter how white he looked, society and even his family is going to look at him as a black person. He realized that he wasn't going to get the same priviledged as white people got.<br /><br />It wasn't until the last occassion in Paul's life, that paul thought to himself its time to change my life, and live it as a black man. Paul put all of his childhood memories behind him except for those that taught his him life long lessons. And he went on to survive with only his skills with and his friend Mitchell.<br /><br />I could go in more detail but I don't want to give away details. This book is very detailed and well written and the detail allowed me to put myself in Paul's shoes and experience all that he did. At times I got mad with Paul, I got sad with Paul, I even got happy with Paul. And being allowed to do that just made this book even better. I recommend this book to those who needs a good read that doesn't only entertain you but teaches you lessons as you read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15503721797624025832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_573546642" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/573546642" />
    <a title="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard"><img alt="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1321462468p2/2216677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/573546642?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cassi aka Snow White Haggard" href="/user/show/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard">Cassi aka Snow White Haggard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2216677-cassi-aka-snow-white-haggard?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer573546642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13602247059183890168">The Land is a young adult classic that sadly I never encountered in my youth. It takes place in a post-Civil War South. Paul Edward is the son of a former slave owner. Unlike most blacks boys, Paul's father acknowledges him, educated him in a time when it was illegal for blacks to have an education and treats him as his own. In some ways that sounds wonderful, but in other ways it makes it more difficult for Paul to live as a black man (even though he can pass for white) in the South because he </span>
  <span id="freeText13602247059183890168" style="display:none">The Land is a young adult classic that sadly I never encountered in my youth. It takes place in a post-Civil War South. Paul Edward is the son of a former slave owner. Unlike most blacks boys, Paul's father acknowledges him, educated him in a time when it was illegal for blacks to have an education and treats him as his own. In some ways that sounds wonderful, but in other ways it makes it more difficult for Paul to live as a black man (even though he can pass for white) in the South because he was not raised as most black boys are raised.<br /><br />This book has all the themes that classic Southern tales have, racism, hatred, poverty, etc. But it's just as much about family as anything else. For me the family story was heartbreaking, resonating and stayed with me. <br /><br />A timeless tale, The Land will make your heart hurt and you'll probably shed a few tears. But it's not a downtrodden, sad story, it's a hopeful story where a boy becomes a man and builds a live for himself on his own terms. It's a book about finding your own way in the world, becoming a self-made man, and making something out of nothing. Even though it may taken place in the post-Civil War South, the themes transcend the setting, creating an ageless book.<br /><br /><b>Narration</b><br />It's hard for me to seperation the narration from the story. The narration is wonderful and perfect for the story. I can still hear Paul Edwards deep voice in my head and it will always be how I imagine Paul Edward. If you find this audiobook listen to it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13602247059183890168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_475733749" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/475733749" />
    <a title="Emma Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15399188-emma-lauren"><img alt="Emma Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1370399132p2/15399188.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/475733749?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Lauren" href="/user/show/15399188-emma-lauren">Emma Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780439442411" href="/book/show/2628565-the-land">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer475733749" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11613494777953264495">The Land by Mildred D. Taylor, was the prequel to the critically acclaimed novel, Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry. I read Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry, when I was very young, eleven years old to be exact, and some of the concepts were much more difficult to understand than they are now. Therefore, I reread the novel when I was thirteen, and absolutely loved it, and have purchased several novels in this series. This, being the prequel, was the story of Cassie's grandfather, and how his story truly c</span>
  <span id="freeText11613494777953264495" style="display:none">The Land by Mildred D. Taylor, was the prequel to the critically acclaimed novel, Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry. I read Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry, when I was very young, eleven years old to be exact, and some of the concepts were much more difficult to understand than they are now. Therefore, I reread the novel when I was thirteen, and absolutely loved it, and have purchased several novels in this series. This, being the prequel, was the story of Cassie's grandfather, and how his story truly came to be. This book was rich with symbolism, and real-life aspects, and it had twists and turns that every reader can love in a historical-fiction novel. What I did not know about this book, was that it is based on the true events of Taylor's life, and her family's lives, and that just makes this story all that much more better. The fact to see the cruelty and the honesty in people, all at the same time, within paragraphs of each other, is amazing. This book is great, and it is clear what it received a Coretta Scott King Award.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11613494777953264495" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Hastings75" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50092184-hastings75"><img alt="Hastings75" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450484494p2/50092184.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1734327299?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hastings75" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hastings75" href="/user/show/50092184-hastings75">Hastings75</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50092184-hastings75?shelf=read-harder-2016">read-harder-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1734327299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13217452908042680197">This has to be one of my favourite reads of the year!<br/><br/>Loved Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry as a child and was excited to hear that this prequel (and a couple of sequels) existed. Thanks to the Read Harder Challenge (and the redhead) for steering me in the direction of this "very fine" novel!<br/><br/>The lead character and narrator is entirely believable and despite his trials and tribulations behaves in a way that is consistent with his character. I liked the fact that the good guys don't always win and the</span>
  <span id="freeText13217452908042680197" style="display:none">This has to be one of my favourite reads of the year!<br /><br />Loved Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry as a child and was excited to hear that this prequel (and a couple of sequels) existed. Thanks to the Read Harder Challenge (and the redhead) for steering me in the direction of this "very fine" novel!<br /><br />The lead character and narrator is entirely believable and despite his trials and tribulations behaves in a way that is consistent with his character. I liked the fact that the good guys don't always win and the bad guys don't always lose. A perfectly believable situation when you realise that you are essentially reliving an era that saw the emancipation of slaves after the Civil War.<br /><br />Without wanting to give away any spoilers, I will finish my review by saying that about halfway through the novel, it occurred to me that the dream for The Land that Paul Edward unwaveringly had tied in nicely to MLK's famous "I have a Dream" speech. <br /><br />Bring on the next novel in the series!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13217452908042680197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_237862590" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/237862590" />
    <a title="Jewell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1542509-jewell"><img alt="Jewell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412090434p2/1542509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/237862590?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jewell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jewell" href="/user/show/1542509-jewell">Jewell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer237862590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2955234480203909999">Mildred Taylor is a treasure. THE LAND, a prequel to ROLL OF THUNDER, HEAR MY CRY is a rich, complex story about a mixed race, former slave, Paul Edward, who forges his destiny in post-Civil War Georgia. Adults and young adults will find this tale satisfying because of Ms. Taylor's fine dialogue and compelling characterizations. This story, based on Ms. Taylor's great-grandparents, relives the drama of ex-slaves's trying to get a stake hold in America as free men and women.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2853171479" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2853171479" />
    <a title="Jodie Pine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2878385-jodie-pine"><img alt="Jodie Pine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534041177p2/2878385.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2853171479?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jodie Pine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jodie Pine" href="/user/show/2878385-jodie-pine">Jodie Pine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2853171479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13517920963419074269">Mildred D Taylor is a master storyteller and is incredibly gifted in character development. Our family has been captivated by the Logan family's generational story as we have read her books outloud. The Land gives insightful background to the book we started with--Roll of Thunder Hear My Cry--and a greater understanding of why fighting to hold on to the land was so important to Cassie's family. <br/><br/>The way Taylor brings out racial issues allows the reader to ponder them from different angles. In thi</span>
  <span id="freeText13517920963419074269" style="display:none">Mildred D Taylor is a master storyteller and is incredibly gifted in character development. Our family has been captivated by the Logan family's generational story as we have read her books outloud. The Land gives insightful background to the book we started with--Roll of Thunder Hear My Cry--and a greater understanding of why fighting to hold on to the land was so important to Cassie's family. <br /><br />The way Taylor brings out racial issues allows the reader to ponder them from different angles. In this story Paul, with his former slave mother and white landowner father, has a foot in both black and white worlds but isn't actually accepted in either. Because of his skin color, he faces great challenges and injustices; his journey is both gripping and inspirational.<br /><br />In her Acknowledgments section, Taylor highlights the impact of passing down family stories. During a family gathering, she recorded her uncles' story telling, which provided the remaining material she needed for The Land. Her editor insisted, when the writing became difficult, that The Land was a story Taylor "had to write, for no one else could." After three years she thought the book was done but her editor said it was a great beginning. "Four years later," Taylor wrote, "I think it is."<br /><br />In her author's note at the end, she said: "I am grateful to my great-grandparents for leaving such a legacy. I am grateful as well to all those who passed it on. I am especially grateful to my mother, who has always had faith in me and my dreams, and who gave so much to save the mountain land, thus furthering the legacy, and to my father, who more than anyone made me so aware of my heritage. As I have said many times before, without my father's words, my words would not have been. I consider myself blessed to be able to share my family's legacy with all who read my books."</span>
  <a data-text-id="13517920963419074269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28374194-booksbythecup?shelf=2020-read">2020-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3151583965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8717450815891080474">“We were all connected, but the family line was muddled by color, and as I grew older, things began to take on different meanings for me.” —The Land, Mildred D. Taylor<br/><br/>Thank you to Adira @introvertinterrupted for bringing to my attention that Mildred Taylor had written several books about the Logan family. I had no idea there was a series for the popular book, Roll of Thunder Hear my Cry until I saw several of her posts earlier this year. At that moment, I was determined to get my hands on them a</span>
  <span id="freeText8717450815891080474" style="display:none">“We were all connected, but the family line was muddled by color, and as I grew older, things began to take on different meanings for me.” —The Land, Mildred D. Taylor<br /><br />Thank you to Adira @introvertinterrupted for bringing to my attention that Mildred Taylor had written several books about the Logan family. I had no idea there was a series for the popular book, Roll of Thunder Hear my Cry until I saw several of her posts earlier this year. At that moment, I was determined to get my hands on them and read them all.<br /><br />These books are primarily based on Taylor's own family. Since I want to read Roll of Thunder I decided to start at the beginning although I might not read them all in order.<br /><br />What I enjoyed most about the book was seeing life through the eyes of Paul. Life as a slave has to be complicated enough, but this family dynamic and its affects are quite challenging for young Paul. Being a fair skin black boy, the offspring of a white father, Edward Logan, who owns Paul, his sister Cassie and his mother.<br /><br />Right is right and wrong is wrong, but he soon comes to understand that his life, as a black person, will always be different than that of his white brothers.<br /><br />Paul learns difficult lessons, lessons that still ring true even today. That he isn't viewed as an equal and the best way he can survive, is to use his head. Not his emotions. For him to understand who he is and what that means for him. Injustice is not right or fair, but from the perspective of a young person, it feels even more complicated, and just simply, wrong.<br /><br />I'm looking forward to reading the rest of the books but might have to jump ahead and read Roll of Thunder (my library hold is in) and come back to the remaining books.<br />-<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8717450815891080474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2303572384" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6737400243255700896">The Land starts during the younger childhood of Paul-Edward Logan. Paul has lived on his rich white daddy's farm during all of his life. His mother who was once a slave to Edward Logan had him and his older sister Cassie. Paul's father had 3 other children with a different woman and Paul has been close with his 3 brothers all of his life. Through out the book it tells of his hardships of a colored man with an education and a lust for land of his own. It also tells of how hard it was to be colore</span>
  <span id="freeText6737400243255700896" style="display:none">The Land starts during the younger childhood of Paul-Edward Logan. Paul has lived on his rich white daddy's farm during all of his life. His mother who was once a slave to Edward Logan had him and his older sister Cassie. Paul's father had 3 other children with a different woman and Paul has been close with his 3 brothers all of his life. Through out the book it tells of his hardships of a colored man with an education and a lust for land of his own. It also tells of how hard it was to be colored but look to be white. <br /> In The Land people judged Paul because of his skin color. This still happens in the real world today: people are judged because of things that they can't change instead of by who they are as a person. In the book this isn't really fixed because that isn't something that you can control, Paul just tries to stay away from white men and never fully trust another man other than a select two or three. In the real world this still isn't wholly fixed however people of color are being given the same rights as white people.<br /> I really enjoyed this book it had a very real feel to it however I did not love the pacing of the book. It was not a book that you wanted to read all the time and would keep you captivated at all times. It just kind of plodded along at a relatively slow pace. I liked the authenticity of the characters and the whole story line it was just a little boring. If you want a nice relaxing book about cutting trees and the hardships of life as a colored man then I totally recommend it, However if you are looking for good action then you might not love it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6737400243255700896" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Never Without a Book" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Never Without a Book" href="/user/show/45952189-never-without-a-book">Never Without a Book</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5880096804864642867">I am happy to say that I LOVED this book!⁣<br/><br/>Initially I was worried that I would be disappointed with The Land, because Roll of Thunder was the only book by Taylor that I’ve read It’s my absolute favorite. In this book Taylor plants the seed for the Logan family series and focuses on, Paul-Edward Logan— who was Born into slavery a little before the end of the civil war. Paul-Edward’s father, Edward Logan, is a wealthy white landowner and widower with three white sons. Now, Paul-Edward, his mother </span>
  <span id="freeText5880096804864642867" style="display:none">I am happy to say that I LOVED this book!⁣<br /><br />Initially I was worried that I would be disappointed with The Land, because Roll of Thunder was the only book by Taylor that I’ve read It’s my absolute favorite. In this book Taylor plants the seed for the Logan family series and focuses on, Paul-Edward Logan— who was Born into slavery a little before the end of the civil war. Paul-Edward’s father, Edward Logan, is a wealthy white landowner and widower with three white sons. Now, Paul-Edward, his mother and sister Cassie, live in a small house on the Logan estate. ⁣<br />⁣<br />Knowing what I know about slave owners and their Black mistress, this next part of the story took me by surprise. Edward Logan allowed Paul-Edward and Cassie to eat at his table alongside their white siblings and he taught them how to read and write, although it is against the law.⁣<br />⁣<br />Wait, what?!!!! At this point Taylor had my full attention. Paul-Edward can easily pass for white and through the book we see Paul face the struggles of the color line. Y’all, I ate this book up! Based on the experiences of her family, Taylor has shared some essentially Black history in her works and that why this was an easy 5/5 stars read. Now I’m excited for the next book in the series, Song of the Trees.⁣</span>

<div id="review_3022218834" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3022218834" />
    <a title="Owen Marshall" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/104248314-owen-marshall"><img alt="Owen Marshall" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3022218834?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Owen Marshall" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Owen Marshall" href="/user/show/104248314-owen-marshall">Owen Marshall</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3022218834&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3022218834" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13435670010384254241">Owen Marshall <br/>Period 6, Mr.Patera/ Ms.O'brien <br/><br/><br/><br/>The Land written by Mildered D. Taylor published july 5th 2000; Was written about about a man named Pual-Edward Logan and his life and family until he was a grown man. I loved this book because it talks about Paul's life as a kid growing up on his white dad’s land while he was mixed. This book gives voice to what life was like after the civil war and what it was like to be black and well educated during this time period. <br/><br/> The Land took place near the</span>
  <span id="freeText13435670010384254241" style="display:none">Owen Marshall <br />Period 6, Mr.Patera/ Ms.O'brien <br /><br /><br /><br />The Land written by Mildered D. Taylor published july 5th 2000; Was written about about a man named Pual-Edward Logan and his life and family until he was a grown man. I loved this book because it talks about Paul's life as a kid growing up on his white dad’s land while he was mixed. This book gives voice to what life was like after the civil war and what it was like to be black and well educated during this time period. <br /><br /> The Land took place near the end of the 1800’s and early 1900’s. The book followed Paul throughout his life, Paul grew up in Georgia then from there he went to East Texas where he looked into purchasing horses with his father Edward. From there he ran away from home with a boy named Mitchell who also lived and worked on Edward’s land. Mitchell and Paul left East Texas to start a new life because Paul raced a horse for a man named Ray Sutcliffe, Ray promised Paul four times a riders pay if he won. Paul being a very experienced rider, won. Ray hadn't paid Paul the money he deserved and because Paul and Mitchell were people of color, they were unable to collect. Paul decided not to take further action, later on while Paul was resting he had seen Mitchell sprinting at him he asked what had happened and Mitchell had said he took the money that paul had won. In a panic the two boys were looking for a place to hide because the punishment for stealing from a white man would have been death. They got on a train with a woman who offered Paul a job earlier and she hid them from Ray and the other white men looking for them. The boys getting on that train heading through the deep south would change their life forever. Paul and Mitchell spent the next several years working at lumber camps together as young teenagers, continually being faced with racism. Paul dreamt about owning a large piece of land like his father. After years of working in camps for racist and unjust bosses, Paul decides to go into a small town called Vicksburg and find a job. Paul meets a man named Luke Sawyer and begins work as a woodworker, he was a very talented due to his dad sending him to train as a woodworker when he was younger. Because of the quality of Paul’s work, Luke contracted him, and for a year Paul would have success. A new chapter in paul's life started, which led to new challenges and harder work than he had ever experienced, his past experiences, knowledge, and determination would help guide him. <br /><br /> The book The Land was one of the best books I’ve ever read, it goes into detail about the struggles and hardships of a young man named Pual Logan. Something I really enjoyed was how Paul faced adversity but when most people would give up or quit, he would persist on for what he believed in. He was a strong-willed man with a lot of faith, it is truly an inspirational book, and it is an example of what people should aspire to be like. There was never a moment that I wanted to put this book down. I genuinely enjoyed learning about Paul-Edward Logan's perseverance, and it has inspired me to see what real hard work is and how I can carry it over into my life today.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13435670010384254241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8375599379100048666">This was amazing. Thoroughly loved it. Being half black, half white, it was easy for me to identify with the main character. I don't think there's enough written (at least that I know of) regarding the situation of interracial people during the era of the reconstruction. The complexity of their situation then and now seems largely overlooked. So, for that reason alone I loved the attention this gave the topic. But, wow, there were great lessons to learn here - family, friendship, loyalty, patien</span>
  <span id="freeText8375599379100048666" style="display:none">This was amazing. Thoroughly loved it. Being half black, half white, it was easy for me to identify with the main character. I don't think there's enough written (at least that I know of) regarding the situation of interracial people during the era of the reconstruction. The complexity of their situation then and now seems largely overlooked. So, for that reason alone I loved the attention this gave the topic. But, wow, there were great lessons to learn here - family, friendship, loyalty, patience, stick-to-it-tiveness, industry, prayer - it's all here. One of the best stories I've read to the kids. And they loved it too! Very good! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8710521069745619699">This is the first book (though written later, I believe) in the story of the Logan family, which includes Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry. I read that one first and wanted to go back in the family history so I grabbed this one next.<br/><br/>The novel heavily involves race relations in the immediate post-slavery years, so it has quite a bit of uncomfortable subject matter. It’s an incredibly good book and worth the time. I also loved at the end of the book when the author talked about how much of the story w</span>
  <span id="freeText8710521069745619699" style="display:none">This is the first book (though written later, I believe) in the story of the Logan family, which includes Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry. I read that one first and wanted to go back in the family history so I grabbed this one next.<br /><br />The novel heavily involves race relations in the immediate post-slavery years, so it has quite a bit of uncomfortable subject matter. It’s an incredibly good book and worth the time. I also loved at the end of the book when the author talked about how much of the story was based on her own family history.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittany" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittany" href="/user/show/6281242-brittany">Brittany</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3260677003" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11022374976628454307">Not sure how I’ve never heard of this book but this book blew me away, despite the terrible cover. So glad that didn’t turn me away. I want to read the entire series right away and can’t wait until the next one shows up. At 400 pages, it’s not a short read but it’s so well-developed and you cannot help but root for Paul-Edward from the first page. Absolutely worth the read. Make sure to read the author’s note at the end, as well.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lvEIzsCwldsYckYt8mZnGKzk4ehqqoLjeVH+4Q08nRSqHuOd5/hwWGDUnqs2nXW6p5VrrbRQBjoclD9l3SCMDw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yDamEgn7lxGT+cCydpiTT/XGwOCZbCq43bR9gn0ie6b02U1BLrNykutfGDSyY4Ht/rdKpUeWrmG4cbwGrT5qvQ==')})
  }

The Dionne Quintuplets became a more popular attraction than Niagara Falls, ogled through one-way screens by sightseers as they splashed in their wading pool at the center of a tourist hotspot known as Quintland.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/26946.Mildred_D_Taylor">About Mildred D. Taylor</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/26946.Mildred_D_Taylor"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1472717617p3/26946.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2192461602221374085">Mildred DeLois Taylor is an African-American writer known for her works exploring the struggle faced by African-American families in the Deep South.<br/><br/>Taylor was born in Jackson, Mississippi, but lived there only a short amount of time, then moved to Toledo, Ohio, where she spent most of her childhood. She now lives in Colorado with her daughter. <br/><br/>Many of her works are based on stories of her family t</span>
  <span id="freeText2192461602221374085" style="display:none">Mildred DeLois Taylor is an African-American writer known for her works exploring the struggle faced by African-American families in the Deep South.<br /><br />Taylor was born in Jackson, Mississippi, but lived there only a short amount of time, then moved to Toledo, Ohio, where she spent most of her childhood. She now lives in Colorado with her daughter. <br /><br />Many of her works are based on stories of her family that she heard while growing up. She has stated that these anecdotes became very clear in her mind, and in fact, once she realized that adults talked about the past, "I began to visualize all the family who had once known the land, and I felt as if I knew them, too ..." Taylor has talked about how much history was in the stories; some stories took place during times of slavery and some post-slavery.<br /><br />Taylor's most famous book is <em>Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry</em>. In 1977, the book won the Newbery Medal. <em>Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry</em> is the middle book, chronologically, in the Logans series that also includes titles such as <em>The Land</em>, <em>Song of the Trees</em>, <em>Let the Circle Be Unbroken</em>, and <em>The Road to Memphis</em>. Her collective contributions to children's literature resulted in her being awarded the inaugural NSK Neustadt Prize for Children's Literature in 2003.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2192461602221374085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

Taylor<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.24 avg rating &mdash; 529 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2020\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer4241029779741798448\">The saga of the Logan family--made famous in the Newbery Medal-winning Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry--concludes in a long-awaited and deeply fulfilling story.\n\nIn her tenth book, Mildred Taylor completes her sweeping saga about the Logan family of Mis<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText4241029779741798448\" style=\"display:none\">The saga of the Logan family--made famous in the Newbery Medal-winning Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry--concludes in a long-awaited and deeply fulfilling story.\n\nIn her tenth book, Mildred Taylor completes her sweeping saga about the Logan family of Mississippi, which is also the story of the civil rights movement in America of the 20th century. Cassie Logan, first met in Song of the Trees and Roll of Thunder, Hear My Cry, is a young woman now, searching for her place in the world, a journey that takes her from Toledo to California, to law school in Boston, and, ultimately, in the 60s, home to Mississippito participate in voter registration. She is witness to the now-historic events of the century: the Great Migration north, the rise of the civil rights movement, preceded and precipitated by the racist society of America, and the often violent confrontations that brought about change. Rich, compelling storytelling is Ms. Taylor\'s hallmark, and she fulfills expectations as she brings to a close the stirring family story that has absorbed her for over forty years. It is a story she was born to tell.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"4241029779741798448\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div
